Ephemeral resources always produce ephemeral values.\\n5:  - **Ephemeral values**: Input variables and outputs can now be defined as ephemeral. Ephemeral values may only be used in certain contexts in Terraform configuration, and are not persisted to the plan or state files.\\n6:     - **`ephemeralasnull` function**: a function takes a value of any type and returns a similar value of the same type with any ephemeral values replaced with non-ephemeral null values and all non-ephemeral values preserved.\\n7: \\n8: BUG FIXES:\\n9: \\n10: - The `secret_suffix` in the `kubernetes` backend now includes validation to prevent errors when the `secret_suffix` ends with a number ([#35666](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35666)).\\n11: - The error message for an invalid default value for an input variable now indicates when the problem is with a nested value in a complex data type. ([#35465](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35465))\\n12: - Sensitive marks could be incorrectly transferred to nested resource values, causing erroneous changes during a plan ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\\n13: - Allow unknown `error_message` values to pass the core validate step, so variable validation can be completed later during plan\\n14:   ([#35537](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35537))\\n15: - Unencoded slashes within GitHub module source refs were being truncated and incorrectly used as subdirectories in the request path ([#35552](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35552))\\n16: - Terraform refresh-only plans with output only changes are now applyable. ([#35812](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35812))\\n17: - Postconditions referencing `self` with many instances could encounter an error during evaluation ([#35895](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35895))\\n18: - The `plantimestamp()` function would return an invalid date during validation ([#35902](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35902))\\n19: - Updates to resources which were forced to use create_before_destroy could lose that flag in the state temporarily and cause cycles if immediately removed from the configuration ([#35966](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35966))\\n20: - backend/cloud: Prefer KV tags, even when tags are defined as set ([#35937](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35937))\\n21: - Simplify config generation (`plan -generate-config-out`) for string attributes that contain primitive types (e.g. numbers or booleans) ([#35984](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35984))\\n22: - config: `issensitive` could incorrectly assert that an unknown value was not sensitive during plan, but later became sensitive during apply, causing failures where changes did not match the planned result ([#36012](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36012))\\n23: - config: The evaluation of conditional expressions and for expression in HCL could lose marks with certain combinations of unknown values ([#36017](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36017))\\n24: \\n25: ENHANCEMENTS:\\n26: \\n27: - The `element` function now accepts negative indices ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\\n28: - Import block validation has been improved to provide more useful errors and catch more invalid cases during `terraform validate` ([#35543](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35543))\\n29: - Performance enhancements for resource evaluation, especially when large numbers of resource instances are involved ([#35558](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35558))\\n30: - The `plan`, `apply`, and `refresh` commands now produce a deprecated warning when using the `-state` flag. Instead use the `path` attribute within the `local` backend to modify the state file. ([#35660](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35660))\\n31: - backend/cos: Add new auth for Tencent Cloud backend ([#35888](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35888))\\n32: \\n33: UPGRADE NOTES:\\n34: \\n35: - backend/s3: Removes deprecated attributes for assuming IAM role. Must use the `assume_role` block ([#35721](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35721))\\n36: - backend/s3: The s3 backend now supports S3 native state locking. When used with DynamoDB-based locking, locks will be acquired from both sources. In a future minor release of Terraform the DynamoDB locking mechanism and associated arguments will be deprecated. ([#35661](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35661))\\n37: - `moved`: Moved blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses. Configurations that reference resources with type names that match top level blocks and keywords from `moved` blocks will need to prepend the `resource.` identifier to these references. ([#35850](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35850))\\n38: - config: In order to ensure consistency in results from HCL conditional expressions, marks must be combined from all values within the expression to avoid losing mark information. This typically improves accuracy when validating configuration, but users may see sensitive results where they were lost previously.\\n39: \\n40: ## Previous Releases\\n41: \\n42: For information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\\n43: \\n44: - **Ephemeral resources**: Ephemeral resources are read anew during each phase of Terraform evaluation, and cannot be persisted to state storage. Ephemeral resources always produce ephemeral values.\\n5:  - **Ephemeral values**: Input variables and outputs can now be defined as ephemeral. Ephemeral values may only be used in certain contexts in Terraform configuration, and are not persisted to the plan or state files.\\n6:     - **`ephemeralasnull` function**: a function takes a value of any type and returns a similar value of the same type with any ephemeral values replaced with non-ephemeral null values and all non-ephemeral values preserved.\\n7: \\n8: BUG FIXES:\\n9: \\n10: - The `secret_suffix` in the `kubernetes` backend now includes validation to prevent errors when the `secret_suffix` ends with a number ([#35666](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35666)).\\n11: - The error message for an invalid default value for an input variable now indicates when the problem is with a nested value in a complex data type. ([#35465](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35465))\\n12: - Sensitive marks could be incorrectly transferred to nested resource values, causing erroneous changes during a plan ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\\n13: - Allow unknown `error_message` values to pass the core validate step, so variable validation can be completed later during plan\\n14:   ([#35537](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35537))\\n15: - Unencoded slashes within GitHub module source refs were being truncated and incorrectly used as subdirectories in the request path ([#35552](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35552))\\n16: - Terraform refresh-only plans with output only changes are now applyable. ([#35812](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35812))\\n17: - Postconditions referencing `self` with many instances could encounter an error during evaluation ([#35895](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35895))\\n18: - The `plantimestamp()` function would return an invalid date during validation ([#35902](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35902))\\n19: - Updates to resources which were forced to use create_before_destroy could lose that flag in the state temporarily and cause cycles if immediately removed from the configuration ([#35966](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35966))\\n20: - backend/cloud: Prefer KV tags, even when tags are defined as set ([#35937](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35937))\\n21: - Simplify config generation (`plan -generate-config-out`) for string attributes that contain primitive types (e.g. numbers or booleans) ([#35984](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35984))\\n22: - config: `issensitive` could incorrectly assert that an unknown value was not sensitive during plan, but later became sensitive during apply, causing failures where changes did not match the planned result ([#36012](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36012))\\n23: - config: The evaluation of conditional expressions and for expression in HCL could lose marks with certain combinations of unknown values ([#36017](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36017))\\n24: \\n25: ENHANCEMENTS:\\n26: \\n27: - The `element` function now accepts negative indices ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\\n28: - Import block validation has been improved to provide more useful errors and catch more invalid cases during `terraform validate` ([#35543](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35543))\\n29: - Performance enhancements for resource evaluation, especially when large numbers of resource instances are involved ([#35558](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35558))\\n30: - The `plan`, `apply`, and `refresh` commands now produce a deprecated warning when using the `-state` flag. Instead use the `path` attribute within the `local` backend to modify the state file. ([#35660](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35660))\\n31: - backend/cos: Add new auth for Tencent Cloud backend ([#35888](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35888))\\n32: \\n33: UPGRADE NOTES:\\n34: \\n35: - backend/s3: Removes deprecated attributes for assuming IAM role. Must use the `assume_role` block ([#35721](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35721))\\n36: - backend/s3: The s3 backend now supports S3 native state locking. When used with DynamoDB-based locking, locks will be acquired from both sources. In a future minor release of Terraform the DynamoDB locking mechanism and associated arguments will be deprecated. ([#35661](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35661))\\n37: - `moved`: Moved blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses. Configurations that reference resources with type names that match top level blocks and keywords from `moved` blocks will need to prepend the `resource.` identifier to these references. ([#35850](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35850))\\n38: - config: In order to ensure consistency in results from HCL conditional expressions, marks must be combined from all values within the expression to avoid losing mark information. This typically improves accuracy when validating configuration, but users may see sensitive results where they were lost previously.\\n39: \\n40: ## Previous Releases\\n41: \\n42: For information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\\n43: \\n44: - [v1.9](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.9/CHANGELOG.md)\\n45: - [v1.8](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.8/CHANGELOG.md)\\n46: - [v1.7](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.7/CHANGELOG.md)\\n47: - [v1.6](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.6/CHANGELOG.md)\\n48: - [v1.5](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.5/CHANGELOG.md)\\n49: - [v1.4](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.4/CHANGELOG.md)\\n50: - [v1.3](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.3/CHANGELOG.md)\\n51: - [v1.2](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.2/CHANGELOG.md)\\n52: - [v1.1](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.1/CHANGELOG.md)\\n53: - [v1.0](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.0/CHANGELOG.md)\\n54: - [v0.15](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.15/CHANGELOG.md)\\n55: - [v0.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.14/CHANGELOG.md)\\n56: - [v0.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.13/CHANGELOG.md)\\n57: - [v0.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.12/CHANGELOG.md)\\n58: - [v0.11 and earlier](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.11/CHANGELOG.md)\\n59: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/terraform--24236f4f@e1a7505de5f9af1ffec8078d6baa58426aa7c353/-/blob/CHANGELOG.md%3FL1-200\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: ## 1.10.0 (November 27, 2024)\n2: \n3: NEW FEATURES:\n4:  - **Ephemeral resources**: Ephemeral resources are read anew during each phase of Terraform evaluation, and cannot be persisted to state storage. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01SAsReRVhEhc7NJXvwHEx2t","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01W9anUYKSTZmdKo7BpNCZ7R","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 is a minor release in the stable Terraform v1.0 series and honors the [Terraform v1.0 Compatibility Promises](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1-compatibility-promises). While most configurations will continue to work without modification, this guide covers the breaking changes and new features that may require updates to your configurations.\n\n**Major themes in v1.10.0:**\n- **S3 Backend restructuring** - Removal of deprecated IAM role attributes and introduction of S3 native state locking\n- **Moved blocks syntax enforcement** - Reserved keywords now require explicit `resource.` identifier\n- **Improved sensitive value handling** - Better mark propagation in conditional expressions\n- **Ephemeral values** (new feature) - Support for temporary, non-persistent data in state/plans\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated IAM Role Assumption Attributes\n\n#### What Changed\n\nIn v1.9.0, the S3 backend supported two ways to configure IAM role assumption:\n1. The `assume_role` block (preferred)\n2. Flat attributes at the backend level (deprecated)\n\nIn v1.10.0, **all deprecated top-level IAM role assumption attributes have been removed**. You must use the `assume_role` block syntax.\n\n#### Affected Attributes\n\nThe following attributes have been removed and must be migrated:\n\n| Removed Attribute | Replacement |\n|---|---|\n| `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |\n| `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |\n| `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |\n| `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |\n| `assume_role_policy` | `assume_role.policy` |\n| `assume_role_policy_arns` | `assume_role.policy_arns` |\n| `assume_role_tags` | `assume_role.tags` |\n| `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` | `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys` |\n\n#### Migration Instructions\n\n**Before (v1.9.0 - Deprecated):**\n```terraform\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    role_arn       = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n    session_name   = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id    = \"unique-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n    assume_role_policy = jsonencode({...})\n    assume_role_tags = {\n      Environment = \"production\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0 - Required):**\n```terraform\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn          = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n      session_name      = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id       = \"unique-external-id\"\n      duration          = 3600\n      policy            = jsonencode({...})\n      tags = {\n        Environment = \"production\"\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step-by-Step Migration\n\n1. **Review your terraform backend configuration** - Identify all uses of deprecated top-level attributes\n2. **Create the `assume_role` block** - Add an `assume_role {}` block to your backend configuration\n3. **Move each attribute** to the corresponding location inside the block:\n   - Move `role_arn`, `session_name`, and `external_id` directly\n   - Rename `assume_role_duration_seconds` to `duration`\n   - Rename `assume_role_policy` to `policy`\n   - Rename `assume_role_policy_arns` to `policy_arns`\n   - Move `assume_role_tags` to `tags` inside the block\n   - Move `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` to `transitive_tag_keys`\n4. **Remove the old attributes** from the backend root level\n5. **Test your configuration** - Run `terraform init` to verify the backend configuration works\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Forgetting the block structure** - Remember to wrap all assume role settings in an `assume_role { }` block\n- **Missing attribute renames** - `duration`, `policy`, and `policy_arns` have different names than their old equivalents\n- **Environment variable conflicts** - If you use environment variables for these settings, they will no longer be recognized; you'll need to use AWS credential sources instead\n\n---\n\n### 2. S3 Backend: New S3 Native State Locking (Experimental)\n\n#### What Changed\n\nIn v1.10.0, the S3 backend introduces optional **S3 native state locking** as an experimental feature. This allows state to be locked using S3 Object Lock, without requiring DynamoDB. You can use S3 locking alone or alongside DynamoDB locking.\n\n#### New Configuration Option\n\nA new `use_lockfile` attribute is now available:\n\n```terraform\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    use_lockfile   = true  # Enable S3 native state locking\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"  # Optional: can be used alongside\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### How It Works\n\nWhen `use_lockfile` is enabled:\n- A lock file named `<state-file>.tflock` is created in the same S3 location as the state file\n- Locks are acquired from both DynamoDB (if configured) and S3 simultaneously if both are enabled\n- Both locks must be successfully acquired before operations proceed\n\n#### Migration Considerations\n\n**Important:** Future versions of Terraform will deprecate DynamoDB-based locking in favor of S3 native locking. Start planning your migration:\n\n1. **Current state (v1.10.0)**: You can use DynamoDB locking alone, S3 locking alone, or both together\n2. **Future versions**: DynamoDB locking attributes and `dynamodb_table` will be deprecated\n\n#### Step-by-Step Migration Plan\n\n1. **Test S3 native locking** - Enable `use_lockfile = true` alongside your existing DynamoDB configuration to test compatibility\n2. **Monitor lock acquisition** - Watch Terraform operations to ensure locks are acquired successfully from both sources\n3. **Adjust bucket policies** - Ensure your S3 bucket policy permits object lock operations (see below)\n4. **Plan DynamoDB retirement** - Once comfortable with S3 locking, plan to remove `dynamodb_table` in a future version\n\n#### Required S3 Bucket Policies\n\nWhen using S3 native state locking, update your S3 bucket and IAM policies to permit lock file operations:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n  \"Statement\": [\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Action\": [\n        \"s3:GetObject\",\n        \"s3:PutObject\",\n        \"s3:DeleteObject\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-terraform-state/*\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Action\": [\n        \"s3:ListBucket\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-terraform-state\"\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Lock file permissions** - Ensure your S3 bucket permissions allow creation of the `.tflock` file\n- **Object Lock not enabled** - S3 Object Lock may need to be enabled on your bucket for full durability\n- **Inconsistent configuration** - If some team members use `use_lockfile = true` and others don't, locking behavior will be inconsistent\n\n---\n\n### 3. Moved Blocks: Reserved Keywords Now Require `resource.` Prefix\n\n#### What Changed\n\nIn v1.9.0, `moved` blocks accepted resource addresses directly, even if the resource type name matched Terraform reserved keywords (like `local`, `each`, `self`, etc.).\n\nIn v1.10.0, `moved` blocks now enforce the requirement to **explicitly prepend `resource.`** when referencing resources whose type names conflict with top-level keywords.\n\n#### Reserved Keywords Requiring Explicit Prefix\n\nIf your resource type matches any of these keywords, you must prefix references with `resource.`:\n- `count`\n- `each`\n- `local`\n- `module`\n- `path`\n- `self`\n- `terraform`\n- `var`\n- `template`\n- `lazy`\n- `arg`\n\n#### Examples of Affected Configurations\n\n**Problematic scenario:** If you have a provider that defines a resource type called `local`:\n\nBefore (v1.9.0 - May work):\n```terraform\nresource \"local\" \"config\" {\n  # resource configuration\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = local.config\n  to   = local.renamed\n}\n```\n\nAfter (v1.10.0 - Required):\n```terraform\nresource \"local\" \"config\" {\n  # resource configuration\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.config\n  to   = resource.local.renamed\n}\n```\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThis change prevents ambiguity in address parsing. Without the `resource.` prefix, `local.config` could be interpreted as a reference to a local value (`local.config`) rather than a resource (`resource \"local\" \"config\"`).\n\n#### Migration Instructions\n\n1. **Identify affected resources** - Search your codebase for resource types matching the reserved keywords list above\n2. **Find `moved` blocks** referencing these resources - Search for `moved` blocks with `from` or `to` attributes\n3. **Add `resource.` prefix** - Update the references to use `resource.<type>.<name>` format\n4. **Validate configuration** - Run `terraform validate` to ensure all references are correct\n\n#### Step-by-Step Example\n\nIf you have a custom provider with a resource type `template`:\n\n**Before migration:**\n```terraform\nresource \"template\" \"example\" {\n  content = \"...\"\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = template.example\n  to   = template.v2\n}\n```\n\n**After migration:**\n```terraform\nresource \"template\" \"example\" {\n  content = \"...\"\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = resource.template.example\n  to   = resource.template.v2\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Forgetting module references** - If using `module.X.local` in a moved block, you don't need to prefix; only resource type names matching keywords need the prefix\n- **Partial updates** - Update both `from` and `to` addresses if both reference the problematic resource type\n- **Testing after migration** - Always run `terraform plan` after updating moved blocks to verify the references are correct\n\n---\n\n## Sensitive Value Handling\n\n### What Changed\n\nIn v1.10.0, Terraform improved how sensitive marks are propagated through conditional expressions and for expressions. Previously, marks could be **lost** in certain complex expressions. Now, marks are preserved consistently.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\nWhen combining values with different sensitivity marks in conditional expressions, the resulting value might lose its sensitive mark:\n\n```terraform\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type = string\n}\n\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"non_sensitive_key\" {\n  type = string\n}\n\n# In v1.9.0, the result could lose the sensitive mark in certain cases\nlocals {\n  key = var.environment == \"production\" ? var.api_key : var.non_sensitive_key\n  # Result might not be marked as sensitive\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\nSensitive marks are now **consistently combined** across all branches of conditional expressions:\n\n```terraform\n# In v1.10.0, if ANY branch is sensitive, the result is sensitive\nlocals {\n  key = var.environment == \"production\" ? var.api_key : var.non_sensitive_key\n  # Result is ALWAYS marked as sensitive (as expected)\n}\n```\n\n### Impact on Your Configuration\n\n**User-facing impact:**\n- Outputs that reference sensitive values may now correctly show as sensitive (previously might have been exposed)\n- Plans may show more values as sensitive than before\n- Fewer unintended sensitive value exposures in logs\n\n**Workaround if needed:**\nIf you have a legitimate reason to exclude sensitive values from output, use the new `nonsensitive()` function:\n\n```terraform\noutput \"settings\" {\n  # Use nonsensitive() to explicitly remove the sensitive mark\n  # Only do this if you're certain the output doesn't expose secrets\n  value       = nonsensitive(local.key)\n  description = \"Configuration settings\"\n}\n```\n\n### Migration Guidance\n\n1. **Review configuration outputs** - Check if any outputs reference sensitive values\n2. **Run terraform plan** - Compare plans between v1.9.0 and v1.10.0; you may see additional values marked as sensitive\n3. **Use `nonsensitive()` sparingly** - Only use when you're certain the output won't expose sensitive data\n4. **Update CI/CD logs** - If your CI/CD system redacts sensitive outputs, verify it still works correctly\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Impact\n\n### Ephemeral Resources and Values\n\n#### What's New\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces **ephemeral values** - a new way to handle data that should only exist during the current Terraform operation and never be stored in state or plan files.\n\nThree types of ephemeral constructs are now available:\n\n1. **Ephemeral Input Variables** - Variables marked to exclude from state\n2. **Ephemeral Outputs** - Output values that don't persist in state\n3. **Ephemeral Resources** - A new resource mode for short-lived data (provider support required)\n\n#### Ephemeral Input Variables\n\nUse ephemeral input variables for temporary credentials like authentication tokens:\n\n```terraform\nvariable \"api_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true  # New in v1.10.0\n  description = \"Short-lived API token that expires after the operation\"\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # This local becomes implicitly ephemeral because it references an ephemeral variable\n  auth_header = \"Bearer ${var.api_token}\"\n}\n\nresource \"example\" \"resource\" {\n  # Can use ephemeral values in resource configuration\n  auth_token = local.auth_header\n}\n```\n\n#### Ephemeral Outputs\n\nMark outputs as ephemeral to prevent them from being stored in state:\n\n```terraform\noutput \"temporary_token\" {\n  value     = var.api_token\n  ephemeral = true  # New in v1.10.0\n  description = \"Token that expires and is not stored in state\"\n}\n```\n\n#### Valid Contexts for Ephemeral Values\n\nEphemeral values can only be used in specific contexts:\n\n✅ **Valid uses:**\n- Referenced by other ephemeral variables\n- Used in local values (which become implicitly ephemeral)\n- Used in ephemeral resource configurations\n- Used in ephemeral outputs\n\n❌ **Invalid uses:**\n- Regular resource configuration attributes (unless in an ephemeral resource)\n- Regular output values\n- For-each meta-argument\n- Count meta-argument\n\n#### Using `ephemeralasnull()` Function\n\nThe new `ephemeralasnull()` function allows you to convert ephemeral values to null, enabling use in non-ephemeral contexts:\n\n```terraform\nvariable \"secret_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # Mix ephemeral and non-ephemeral values\n  config = {\n    token    = var.secret_token\n    app_name = \"my-app\"\n  }\n}\n\noutput \"config\" {\n  # Use ephemeralasnull to output non-ephemeral values\n  # Ephemeral values become null in the output\n  value = ephemeralasnull(local.config)\n\n  # The output will be:\n  # {\n  #   token    = null  (was ephemeral)\n  #   app_name = \"my-app\"  (preserved)\n  # }\n}\n```\n\n#### Planning for Ephemeral Resource Support\n\nSome providers may add support for ephemeral resource types in the future:\n\n```terraform\nresource \"aws_temporary_credentials\" \"example\" {\n  # Future: providers may support ephemeral resources\n  # These would automatically produce ephemeral values\n  role_arn    = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/temp\"\n  duration_seconds = 3600\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Considerations\n\n**When should you use ephemeral values:**\n- Short-lived credentials (API tokens, temporary passwords)\n- Dynamic secrets that expire\n- Values that should never be persisted\n- Sensitive data that should not appear in state files\n\n**When NOT to use ephemeral values:**\n- Regular configuration that needs to be reproducible\n- Data that must be available in subsequent operations\n- Values needed for state tracking (use `sensitive = true` instead)\n\n#### Important Notes on Ephemeral Values\n\n⚠️ **Ephemeral values during apply:**\n- If an ephemeral variable is used during planning, it must be provided again during apply\n- Ephemeral values are recalculated during apply; they don't use the planned value\n\n⚠️ **State file compatibility:**\n- Ephemeral values are never written to state files\n- If a variable changes from regular to ephemeral, prior state values won't be available\n- Can't reference historical ephemeral values in subsequent operations\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\n### Validation Checklist\n\nUse this checklist to verify your migration:\n\n```bash\n# 1. Validate syntax\nterraform validate\n\n# 2. Check for deprecation warnings\nterraform plan -input=false -out=tfplan\n\n# 3. Review the plan output\nterraform show tfplan\n\n# 4. Verify sensitive values are marked correctly\nterraform plan -json | grep -i sensitive\n\n# 5. Test with actual apply (in non-production first)\nterraform apply tfplan\n\n# 6. Verify state file format\nterraform show\n```\n\n### Step-by-Step Testing Process\n\n**Phase 1: Local Development**\n\n1. Update your terraform configuration files\n2. Run `terraform validate` to catch syntax errors\n3. Run `terraform plan` and review the output\n4. Look for any unexpected changes\n5. Test with `-auto-approve` in a safe environment\n\n**Phase 2: Staging Environment**\n\n1. Apply changes to your staging environment\n2. Monitor for any issues with state locking\n3. Verify S3 lock files are created (if using new locking)\n4. Test plan and apply cycles multiple times\n5. Verify no sensitive values appear in logs\n\n**Phase 3: Production Deployment**\n\n1. Schedule a maintenance window\n2. Ensure all team members are using v1.10.0 or later\n3. Backup your state file\n4. Apply the configuration changes\n5. Monitor for any issues\n6. Document any configuration changes made\n\n### Troubleshooting Common Issues\n\n**Issue: \"Invalid resource address\"**\n\n**Cause:** Resource type matches reserved keyword, missing `resource.` prefix\n\n**Solution:** Add `resource.` prefix to moved block references:\n```terraform\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.old_name  # Add resource. prefix\n  to   = resource.local.new_name\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n**Issue: \"Assume role attributes not supported\"**\n\n**Cause:** Using deprecated top-level assume role attributes in v1.10.0\n\n**Solution:** Migrate to `assume_role` block structure (see S3 Backend Changes section)\n\n---\n\n**Issue: \"S3 lock file permission denied\"**\n\n**Cause:** S3 bucket policy doesn't allow creating `.tflock` files\n\n**Solution:** Update bucket policy to allow `s3:PutObject` and `s3:DeleteObject` on lock files:\n```json\n{\n  \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n  \"Action\": [\n    \"s3:PutObject\",\n    \"s3:DeleteObject\"\n  ],\n  \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-bucket/*.tflock\"\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\nIf you encounter issues with v1.10.0 and need to rollback:\n\n### Quick Rollback\n\n1. **Keep state files intact** - Terraform v1.10.0 is compatible with v1.9.0 state files\n2. **Revert configuration changes** - Restore your `.tf` files to v1.9.0 compatible format\n3. **Switch terraform version** - Use `tfenv` or equivalent to downgrade:\n   ```bash\n   tfenv use 1.9.0\n   ```\n4. **Refresh state** (optional):\n   ```bash\n   terraform refresh\n   ```\n5. **Verify** - Run `terraform plan` to confirm no changes detected\n\n### State File Compatibility\n\n✅ **Safe:** Terraform v1.10.0 can read and work with v1.9.0 state files\n\n✅ **Safe:** Reverting to v1.9.0 after using v1.10.0 is safe (backward compatible)\n\n⚠️ **Caution:** Ephemeral values won't be persisted if reverting to v1.9.0\n\n### Rollback Checklist\n\n- [ ] Stop all terraform operations\n- [ ] Verify your state file is backed up\n- [ ] Revert `*.tf` files to v1.9.0 compatible format\n- [ ] Downgrade terraform binary\n- [ ] Run `terraform plan` to verify no unexpected changes\n- [ ] Document any issues encountered\n- [ ] Communicate with team members\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Version Compatibility\n\n| Feature | v1.9.0 | v1.10.0 |\n|---------|--------|---------|\n| Old S3 assume_role attributes | ✅ Supported | ❌ Removed |\n| `assume_role` block | ✅ Supported | ✅ Supported |\n| S3 native locking (`use_lockfile`) | ❌ Not available | ✅ Available (experimental) |\n| `resource.` prefix in moved blocks | ⚠️ Optional | ✅ Required for reserved keywords |\n| Sensitive mark propagation | ⚠️ Inconsistent | ✅ Consistent |\n| Ephemeral values | ❌ Not available | ✅ Available (beta) |\n| `ephemeralasnull()` function | ❌ Not available | ✅ Available |\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- [Official Terraform Changelog](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [Terraform v1.0 Compatibility Promises](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1-compatibility-promises)\n- [S3 Backend Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/backend/s3)\n- [Moved Block Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/moved)\n- [Ephemeral Values Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/values/variables)\n- [Terraform Community Forum](https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core)\n\n---\n\n## Getting Help\n\nIf you encounter issues during migration:\n\n1. **Consult the changelog** - Check the full CHANGELOG.md for your specific issue\n2. **Enable debug logging** - Set `TF_LOG=DEBUG` for detailed output:\n   ```bash\n   TF_LOG=DEBUG terraform plan\n   ```\n3. **Check your configuration** - Run `terraform validate` to catch syntax errors\n4. **Review error messages carefully** - They often indicate which attribute or block needs fixing\n5. **Ask the community** - Post in the [Terraform Forum](https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core) if stuck\n6. **Report bugs** - File issues on [GitHub](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues)\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":8011,"cache_read_input_tokens":89576,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":8011},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"d0fa1952-ba9f-48c4-bad4-5fd7af00962b","uuid":"07740c75-dffc-48a4-82f1-cc4bcae1f8a3"}

While most configurations will continue to work without modification, this guide covers the breaking changes and new features that may require updates to your configurations.\n\n**Major themes in v1.10.0:**\n- **S3 Backend restructuring** - Removal of deprecated IAM role attributes and introduction of S3 native state locking\n- **Moved blocks syntax enforcement** - Reserved keywords now require explicit `resource.` identifier\n- **Improved sensitive value handling** - Better mark propagation in conditional expressions\n- **Ephemeral values** (new feature) - Support for temporary, non-persistent data in state/plans\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated IAM Role Assumption Attributes\n\n#### What Changed\n\nIn v1.9.0, the S3 backend supported two ways to configure IAM role assumption:\n1. The `assume_role` block (preferred)\n2. Flat attributes at the backend level (deprecated)\n\nIn v1.10.0, **all deprecated top-level IAM role assumption attributes have been removed**. You must use the `assume_role` block syntax.\n\n#### Affected Attributes\n\nThe following attributes have been removed and must be migrated:\n\n| Removed Attribute | Replacement |\n|---|---|\n| `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |\n| `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |\n| `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |\n| `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |\n| `assume_role_policy` | `assume_role.policy` |\n| `assume_role_policy_arns` | `assume_role.policy_arns` |\n| `assume_role_tags` | `assume_role.tags` |\n| `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` | `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys` |\n\n#### Migration Instructions\n\n**Before (v1.9.0 - Deprecated):**\n```terraform\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    role_arn       = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n    session_name   = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id    = \"unique-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n    assume_role_policy = jsonencode({...})\n    assume_role_tags = {\n      Environment = \"production\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0 - Required):**\n```terraform\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn          = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n      session_name      = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id       = \"unique-external-id\"\n      duration          = 3600\n      policy            = jsonencode({...})\n      tags = {\n        Environment = \"production\"\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step-by-Step Migration\n\n1. **Review your terraform backend configuration** - Identify all uses of deprecated top-level attributes\n2. **Create the `assume_role` block** - Add an `assume_role {}` block to your backend configuration\n3. **Move each attribute** to the corresponding location inside the block:\n   - Move `role_arn`, `session_name`, and `external_id` directly\n   - Rename `assume_role_duration_seconds` to `duration`\n   - Rename `assume_role_policy` to `policy`\n   - Rename `assume_role_policy_arns` to `policy_arns`\n   - Move `assume_role_tags` to `tags` inside the block\n   - Move `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` to `transitive_tag_keys`\n4. **Remove the old attributes** from the backend root level\n5. **Test your configuration** - Run `terraform init` to verify the backend configuration works\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Forgetting the block structure** - Remember to wrap all assume role settings in an `assume_role { }` block\n- **Missing attribute renames** - `duration`, `policy`, and `policy_arns` have different names than their old equivalents\n- **Environment variable conflicts** - If you use environment variables for these settings, they will no longer be recognized; you'll need to use AWS credential sources instead\n\n---\n\n### 2. S3 Backend: New S3 Native State Locking (Experimental)\n\n#### What Changed\n\nIn v1.10.0, the S3 backend introduces optional **S3 native state locking** as an experimental feature. This allows state to be locked using S3 Object Lock, without requiring DynamoDB. You can use S3 locking alone or alongside DynamoDB locking.\n\n#### New Configuration Option\n\nA new `use_lockfile` attribute is now available:\n\n```terraform\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    use_lockfile   = true  # Enable S3 native state locking\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"  # Optional: can be used alongside\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### How It Works\n\nWhen `use_lockfile` is enabled:\n- A lock file named `<state-file>.tflock` is created in the same S3 location as the state file\n- Locks are acquired from both DynamoDB (if configured) and S3 simultaneously if both are enabled\n- Both locks must be successfully acquired before operations proceed\n\n#### Migration Considerations\n\n**Important:** Future versions of Terraform will deprecate DynamoDB-based locking in favor of S3 native locking. Start planning your migration:\n\n1. **Current state (v1.10.0)**: You can use DynamoDB locking alone, S3 locking alone, or both together\n2. **Future versions**: DynamoDB locking attributes and `dynamodb_table` will be deprecated\n\n#### Step-by-Step Migration Plan\n\n1. **Test S3 native locking** - Enable `use_lockfile = true` alongside your existing DynamoDB configuration to test compatibility\n2. **Monitor lock acquisition** - Watch Terraform operations to ensure locks are acquired successfully from both sources\n3. **Adjust bucket policies** - Ensure your S3 bucket policy permits object lock operations (see below)\n4. **Plan DynamoDB retirement** - Once comfortable with S3 locking, plan to remove `dynamodb_table` in a future version\n\n#### Required S3 Bucket Policies\n\nWhen using S3 native state locking, update your S3 bucket and IAM policies to permit lock file operations:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n  \"Statement\": [\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Action\": [\n        \"s3:GetObject\",\n        \"s3:PutObject\",\n        \"s3:DeleteObject\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-terraform-state/*\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Action\": [\n        \"s3:ListBucket\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-terraform-state\"\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Lock file permissions** - Ensure your S3 bucket permissions allow creation of the `.tflock` file\n- **Object Lock not enabled** - S3 Object Lock may need to be enabled on your bucket for full durability\n- **Inconsistent configuration** - If some team members use `use_lockfile = true` and others don't, locking behavior will be inconsistent\n\n---\n\n### 3. Moved Blocks: Reserved Keywords Now Require `resource.` Prefix\n\n#### What Changed\n\nIn v1.9.0, `moved` blocks accepted resource addresses directly, even if the resource type name matched Terraform reserved keywords (like `local`, `each`, `self`, etc.).\n\nIn v1.10.0, `moved` blocks now enforce the requirement to **explicitly prepend `resource.`** when referencing resources whose type names conflict with top-level keywords.\n\n#### Reserved Keywords Requiring Explicit Prefix\n\nIf your resource type matches any of these keywords, you must prefix references with `resource.`:\n- `count`\n- `each`\n- `local`\n- `module`\n- `path`\n- `self`\n- `terraform`\n- `var`\n- `template`\n- `lazy`\n- `arg`\n\n#### Examples of Affected Configurations\n\n**Problematic scenario:** If you have a provider that defines a resource type called `local`:\n\nBefore (v1.9.0 - May work):\n```terraform\nresource \"local\" \"config\" {\n  # resource configuration\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = local.config\n  to   = local.renamed\n}\n```\n\nAfter (v1.10.0 - Required):\n```terraform\nresource \"local\" \"config\" {\n  # resource configuration\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.config\n  to   = resource.local.renamed\n}\n```\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThis change prevents ambiguity in address parsing. Without the `resource.` prefix, `local.config` could be interpreted as a reference to a local value (`local.config`) rather than a resource (`resource \"local\" \"config\"`).\n\n#### Migration Instructions\n\n1. **Identify affected resources** - Search your codebase for resource types matching the reserved keywords list above\n2. **Find `moved` blocks** referencing these resources - Search for `moved` blocks with `from` or `to` attributes\n3. **Add `resource.` prefix** - Update the references to use `resource.<type>.<name>` format\n4. **Validate configuration** - Run `terraform validate` to ensure all references are correct\n\n#### Step-by-Step Example\n\nIf you have a custom provider with a resource type `template`:\n\n**Before migration:**\n```terraform\nresource \"template\" \"example\" {\n  content = \"...\"\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = template.example\n  to   = template.v2\n}\n```\n\n**After migration:**\n```terraform\nresource \"template\" \"example\" {\n  content = \"...\"\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = resource.template.example\n  to   = resource.template.v2\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Forgetting module references** - If using `module.X.local` in a moved block, you don't need to prefix; only resource type names matching keywords need the prefix\n- **Partial updates** - Update both `from` and `to` addresses if both reference the problematic resource type\n- **Testing after migration** - Always run `terraform plan` after updating moved blocks to verify the references are correct\n\n---\n\n## Sensitive Value Handling\n\n### What Changed\n\nIn v1.10.0, Terraform improved how sensitive marks are propagated through conditional expressions and for expressions. Previously, marks could be **lost** in certain complex expressions. Now, marks are preserved consistently.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\nWhen combining values with different sensitivity marks in conditional expressions, the resulting value might lose its sensitive mark:\n\n```terraform\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type = string\n}\n\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"non_sensitive_key\" {\n  type = string\n}\n\n# In v1.9.0, the result could lose the sensitive mark in certain cases\nlocals {\n  key = var.environment == \"production\" ? var.api_key : var.non_sensitive_key\n  # Result might not be marked as sensitive\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\nSensitive marks are now **consistently combined** across all branches of conditional expressions:\n\n```terraform\n# In v1.10.0, if ANY branch is sensitive, the result is sensitive\nlocals {\n  key = var.environment == \"production\" ? var.api_key : var.non_sensitive_key\n  # Result is ALWAYS marked as sensitive (as expected)\n}\n```\n\n### Impact on Your Configuration\n\n**User-facing impact:**\n- Outputs that reference sensitive values may now correctly show as sensitive (previously might have been exposed)\n- Plans may show more values as sensitive than before\n- Fewer unintended sensitive value exposures in logs\n\n**Workaround if needed:**\nIf you have a legitimate reason to exclude sensitive values from output, use the new `nonsensitive()` function:\n\n```terraform\noutput \"settings\" {\n  # Use nonsensitive() to explicitly remove the sensitive mark\n  # Only do this if you're certain the output doesn't expose secrets\n  value       = nonsensitive(local.key)\n  description = \"Configuration settings\"\n}\n```\n\n### Migration Guidance\n\n1. **Review configuration outputs** - Check if any outputs reference sensitive values\n2. **Run terraform plan** - Compare plans between v1.9.0 and v1.10.0; you may see additional values marked as sensitive\n3. **Use `nonsensitive()` sparingly** - Only use when you're certain the output won't expose sensitive data\n4. **Update CI/CD logs** - If your CI/CD system redacts sensitive outputs, verify it still works correctly\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Impact\n\n### Ephemeral Resources and Values\n\n#### What's New\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces **ephemeral values** - a new way to handle data that should only exist during the current Terraform operation and never be stored in state or plan files.\n\nThree types of ephemeral constructs are now available:\n\n1. **Ephemeral Input Variables** - Variables marked to exclude from state\n2. **Ephemeral Outputs** - Output values that don't persist in state\n3. **Ephemeral Resources** - A new resource mode for short-lived data (provider support required)\n\n#### Ephemeral Input Variables\n\nUse ephemeral input variables for temporary credentials like authentication tokens:\n\n```terraform\nvariable \"api_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true  # New in v1.10.0\n  description = \"Short-lived API token that expires after the operation\"\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # This local becomes implicitly ephemeral because it references an ephemeral variable\n  auth_header = \"Bearer ${var.api_token}\"\n}\n\nresource \"example\" \"resource\" {\n  # Can use ephemeral values in resource configuration\n  auth_token = local.auth_header\n}\n```\n\n#### Ephemeral Outputs\n\nMark outputs as ephemeral to prevent them from being stored in state:\n\n```terraform\noutput \"temporary_token\" {\n  value     = var.api_token\n  ephemeral = true  # New in v1.10.0\n  description = \"Token that expires and is not stored in state\"\n}\n```\n\n#### Valid Contexts for Ephemeral Values\n\nEphemeral values can only be used in specific contexts:\n\n✅ **Valid uses:**\n- Referenced by other ephemeral variables\n- Used in local values (which become implicitly ephemeral)\n- Used in ephemeral resource configurations\n- Used in ephemeral outputs\n\n❌ **Invalid uses:**\n- Regular resource configuration attributes (unless in an ephemeral resource)\n- Regular output values\n- For-each meta-argument\n- Count meta-argument\n\n#### Using `ephemeralasnull()` Function\n\nThe new `ephemeralasnull()` function allows you to convert ephemeral values to null, enabling use in non-ephemeral contexts:\n\n```terraform\nvariable \"secret_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # Mix ephemeral and non-ephemeral values\n  config = {\n    token    = var.secret_token\n    app_name = \"my-app\"\n  }\n}\n\noutput \"config\" {\n  # Use ephemeralasnull to output non-ephemeral values\n  # Ephemeral values become null in the output\n  value = ephemeralasnull(local.config)\n\n  # The output will be:\n  # {\n  #   token    = null  (was ephemeral)\n  #   app_name = \"my-app\"  (preserved)\n  # }\n}\n```\n\n#### Planning for Ephemeral Resource Support\n\nSome providers may add support for ephemeral resource types in the future:\n\n```terraform\nresource \"aws_temporary_credentials\" \"example\" {\n  # Future: providers may support ephemeral resources\n  # These would automatically produce ephemeral values\n  role_arn    = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/temp\"\n  duration_seconds = 3600\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Considerations\n\n**When should you use ephemeral values:**\n- Short-lived credentials (API tokens, temporary passwords)\n- Dynamic secrets that expire\n- Values that should never be persisted\n- Sensitive data that should not appear in state files\n\n**When NOT to use ephemeral values:**\n- Regular configuration that needs to be reproducible\n- Data that must be available in subsequent operations\n- Values needed for state tracking (use `sensitive = true` instead)\n\n#### Important Notes on Ephemeral Values\n\n⚠️ **Ephemeral values during apply:**\n- If an ephemeral variable is used during planning, it must be provided again during apply\n- Ephemeral values are recalculated during apply; they don't use the planned value\n\n⚠️ **State file compatibility:**\n- Ephemeral values are never written to state files\n- If a variable changes from regular to ephemeral, prior state values won't be available\n- Can't reference historical ephemeral values in subsequent operations\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\n### Validation Checklist\n\nUse this checklist to verify your migration:\n\n```bash\n# 1. Validate syntax\nterraform validate\n\n# 2. Check for deprecation warnings\nterraform plan -input=false -out=tfplan\n\n# 3. Review the plan output\nterraform show tfplan\n\n# 4. Verify sensitive values are marked correctly\nterraform plan -json | grep -i sensitive\n\n# 5. Test with actual apply (in non-production first)\nterraform apply tfplan\n\n# 6. Verify state file format\nterraform show\n```\n\n### Step-by-Step Testing Process\n\n**Phase 1: Local Development**\n\n1. Update your terraform configuration files\n2. Run `terraform validate` to catch syntax errors\n3. Run `terraform plan` and review the output\n4. Look for any unexpected changes\n5. Test with `-auto-approve` in a safe environment\n\n**Phase 2: Staging Environment**\n\n1. Apply changes to your staging environment\n2. Monitor for any issues with state locking\n3. Verify S3 lock files are created (if using new locking)\n4. Test plan and apply cycles multiple times\n5. Verify no sensitive values appear in logs\n\n**Phase 3: Production Deployment**\n\n1. Schedule a maintenance window\n2. Ensure all team members are using v1.10.0 or later\n3. Backup your state file\n4. Apply the configuration changes\n5. Monitor for any issues\n6. Document any configuration changes made\n\n### Troubleshooting Common Issues\n\n**Issue: \"Invalid resource address\"**\n\n**Cause:** Resource type matches reserved keyword, missing `resource.` prefix\n\n**Solution:** Add `resource.` prefix to moved block references:\n```terraform\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.old_name  # Add resource. prefix\n  to   = resource.local.new_name\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n**Issue: \"Assume role attributes not supported\"**\n\n**Cause:** Using deprecated top-level assume role attributes in v1.10.0\n\n**Solution:** Migrate to `assume_role` block structure (see S3 Backend Changes section)\n\n---\n\n**Issue: \"S3 lock file permission denied\"**\n\n**Cause:** S3 bucket policy doesn't allow creating `.tflock` files\n\n**Solution:** Update bucket policy to allow `s3:PutObject` and `s3:DeleteObject` on lock files:\n```json\n{\n  \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n  \"Action\": [\n    \"s3:PutObject\",\n    \"s3:DeleteObject\"\n  ],\n  \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-bucket/*.tflock\"\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\nIf you encounter issues with v1.10.0 and need to rollback:\n\n### Quick Rollback\n\n1. **Keep state files intact** - Terraform v1.10.0 is compatible with v1.9.0 state files\n2. **Revert configuration changes** - Restore your `.tf` files to v1.9.0 compatible format\n3. **Switch terraform version** - Use `tfenv` or equivalent to downgrade:\n   ```bash\n   tfenv use 1.9.0\n   ```\n4. **Refresh state** (optional):\n   ```bash\n   terraform refresh\n   ```\n5. **Verify** - Run `terraform plan` to confirm no changes detected\n\n### State File Compatibility\n\n✅ **Safe:** Terraform v1.10.0 can read and work with v1.9.0 state files\n\n✅ **Safe:** Reverting to v1.9.0 after using v1.10.0 is safe (backward compatible)\n\n⚠️ **Caution:** Ephemeral values won't be persisted if reverting to v1.9.0\n\n### Rollback Checklist\n\n- [ ] Stop all terraform operations\n- [ ] Verify your state file is backed up\n- [ ] Revert `*.tf` files to v1.9.0 compatible format\n- [ ] Downgrade terraform binary\n- [ ] Run `terraform plan` to verify no unexpected changes\n- [ ] Document any issues encountered\n- [ ] Communicate with team members\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Version Compatibility\n\n| Feature | v1.9.0 | v1.10.0 |\n|---------|--------|---------|\n| Old S3 assume_role attributes | ✅ Supported | ❌ Removed |\n| `assume_role` block | ✅ Supported | ✅ Supported |\n| S3 native locking (`use_lockfile`) | ❌ Not available | ✅ Available (experimental) |\n| `resource.` prefix in moved blocks | ⚠️ Optional | ✅ Required for reserved keywords |\n| Sensitive mark propagation | ⚠️ Inconsistent | ✅ Consistent |\n| Ephemeral values | ❌ Not available | ✅ Available (beta) |\n| `ephemeralasnull()` function | ❌ Not available | ✅ Available |\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- [Official Terraform Changelog](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [Terraform v1.0 Compatibility Promises](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1-compatibility-promises)\n- [S3 Backend Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/backend/s3)\n- [Moved Block Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/moved)\n- [Ephemeral Values Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/values/variables)\n- [Terraform Community Forum](https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core)\n\n---\n\n## Getting Help\n\nIf you encounter issues during migration:\n\n1. **Consult the changelog** - Check the full CHANGELOG.md for your specific issue\n2. **Enable debug logging** - Set `TF_LOG=DEBUG` for detailed output:\n   ```bash\n   TF_LOG=DEBUG terraform plan\n   ```\n3. **Check your configuration** -
